colspan="2"></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;padding:0px 2px">\n<p><span class="noprint"><b>History</b> </span></p>\n<ul>\n<li><span class="noprint"><small><a href="/wiki/Meteorological_history_of_Hurricane_Matthew" title="Meteorological history of Hurricane Matthew">Meteorological history</a></small></span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><span class="noprint"><b>Effects</b> </span></p>\n<ul>\n<li><span class="noprint"><small><a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Matthew_in_Haiti" title="Effects of Hurricane Matthew in Haiti">Haiti</a></small></span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><span class="noprint"><b>Other wikis</b> </span></p>\n<ul>\n<li><span class="noprint"><small><a class="extiw" href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Category:Hurricane_Matthew" title="commons:Category:Hurricane Matthew">Commons: Matthew images</a></small></span></li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p><b>Hurricane Matthew</b> was the first <a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_5_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of Category 5 Atlantic hurricanes">Category\xc2\xa05 Atlantic hurricane</a> since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Felix" title="Hurricane Felix">Hurricane Felix</a> in <a href="/wiki/2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2007 Atlantic hurricane season">2007</a>, caused catastrophic damage and a <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_crisis" title="Humanitarian crisis">humanitarian crisis</a> in <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> and also spread widespread damage in the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_United_States" title="Southeastern United States">southeastern United States</a>. The deadliest <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_hurricane" title="Atlantic hurricane">Atlantic hurricane</a> since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Stan" title="Hurricane Stan">Hurricane Stan</a> in <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">2005</a>, Matthew was the thirteenth <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">named storm</a>, fifth <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane" title="Hurricane">hurricane</a> and second <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Major_hurricane" title="Major hurricane">major hurricane</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2016_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2016 Atlantic hurricane season">2016 Atlantic hurricane season</a>. It caused extensive damage to landmasses in the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Antilles" title="Greater Antilles">Greater Antilles</a>, and severe damage in several islands of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a> who were still recovering from <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Joaquin" title="Hurricane Joaquin">Hurricane Joaquin</a> which had pounded such areas nearly a year earlier. At one point, the hurricane even threatened to be the first storm of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SSHS" title="SSHS">Category 3 or higher</a> intensity to strike the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">Hurricane Wilma</a> in 2005, but Matthew stayed just offshore paralleling the <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Floridian coastline</a>.</p>\n<p>Originating from a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> that emerged off Africa on September\xc2\xa022, Matthew developed into a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_storm" title="Tropical storm">tropical storm</a> just east of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> on September\xc2\xa028. It became a hurricane north of <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> on September\xc2\xa029, before undergoing <a href="/wiki/Rapid_intensification" title="Rapid intensification">explosive intensification</a>, ultimately reaching Category\xc2\xa05 intensity on October\xc2\xa01 at just 13.4\xc2\xb0N latitude \xe2\x80\x93 the lowest latitude ever recorded for a storm of this intensity in the Atlantic basin, breaking the record set by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ivan" title="Hurricane Ivan">Hurricane Ivan</a> in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1">[1]</a></sup> Matthew weakened slightly and fluctuated in intensity while making a northward turn toward the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Antilles" title="Greater Antilles">Greater Antilles</a>, remaining a strong Category\xc2\xa04 hurricane as it made its first <a href="/wiki/Landfall" title="Landfall">landfall</a> over Haiti\'s <a href="/wiki/Tiburon_Peninsula" title="Tiburon Peninsula">Tiburon Peninsula</a> early on October\xc2\xa04, and then a second one in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> later that day. Matthew weakened somewhat but re-intensified as it tracked northwest, making landfall in the northern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a>. The storm then paralleled the coast of the southeastern United States over the next 36 hours, gradually weakening while remaining just offshore before making its fourth and final landfall over the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Romain_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Cape Romain National Wildlife Refuge">Cape Romain National Wildlife Refuge</a> near <a href="/wiki/Myrtle_Beach,_South_Carolina" title="Myrtle Beach, South Carolina">Myrtle Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a> as a Category 1 hurricane on the morning of October 8. Matthew re-emerged into the Atlantic shortly afterward, eventually completing its transition into an <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclone</a> as it turned away from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Hatteras,_North_Carolina" title="Cape Hatteras, North Carolina">Cape Hatteras</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> on October\xc2\xa09.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TWC_Storm_History_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-TWC_Storm_History-2">[2]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Widespread effects were felt from Matthew across its destructive path, however, <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Matthew_in_Haiti" title="Effects of Hurricane Matthew in Haiti">the most significant impacts were felt in Haiti</a>, with US$1.9\xc2\xa0billion in damage and 546\xc2\xa0deaths, making Matthew the worst disaster to affect the nation since the <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">2010 earthquake</a>. The combination of flooding and high winds disrupted telecommunications and destroyed extensive swaths of land; around 80% of <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A9r%C3%A9mie" title="J\xc3\xa9r\xc3\xa9mie">J\xc3\xa9r\xc3\xa9mie</a> sustained significant damage. Four people were killed in Cuba due to a bridge collapse, and total losses in the country amounted to US$2.58\xc2\xa0billion, most of which occurred in the Guant\xc3\xa1namo Province. Passing through the Bahamas as a major hurricane, Matthew spread damage across several islands. <a href="/wiki/Grand_Bahama" title="Grand Bahama">Grand Bahama</a> was hit directly, where most homes sustained damage in the townships of Eight Mile Rock and Holmes Rock. Preparations began in earnest across the southeastern United States as Matthew approached, with several states declaring <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">states of emergencies</a> for either entire states or coastal counties; widespread evacuations were ordered for extensive areas of the coast because of predicted high wind speeds and flooding, especially in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jacksonville" title="Jacksonville">Jacksonville</a> Metropolitan Area. In Florida, over 1\xc2\xa0million lost power as the storm passed to the east, with 478,000\xc2\xa0losing power in Georgia and South Carolina. While damage was primarily confined to the coast in Florida and Georgia, torrential rains spread inland in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carolinas" title="Carolinas">Carolinas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, causing widespread flooding.</p>\n<p></p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li class="tocnumber">2.6</span> <span class="toctext">United States</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-10"><a href="#Online_response"><span class="tocnumber">2.6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Online response</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Impact"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Impact</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Lesser_Antilles"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Lesser Antilles</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#ABC_Islands_and_South_America"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">ABC Islands and South America</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Jamaica_2"><span class="tocnumber">3.3</span> <span class="toctext">Jamaica</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Haiti_2"><span class="tocnumber">3.4</span> <span class="toctext">Haiti</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Dominican_Republic_2"><span class="tocnumber">3.5</span> <span class="toctext">Dominican Republic</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Cuba"><span class="tocnumber">3.6</span> <span class="toctext">Cuba</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Bahamas"><span class="tocnumber">3.7</span> <span class="toctext">Bahamas</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#United_States_2"><span class="tocnumber">3.8</span> <span class="toctext">United States</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-20"><a href="#Florida_and_Georgia"><span class="tocnumber">3.8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Florida and Georgia</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-21"><a href="#North_and_South_Carolina"><span class="tocnumber">3.8.2</span> <span class="toctext">North and South Carolina</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-22"><a href="#Virginia_and_the_Northeast"><span class="tocnumber">3.8.3</span> <span class="toctext">Virginia and the Northeast</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Canada"><span class="tocnumber">3.9</span> <span class="toctext">Canada</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Aftermath"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Aftermath</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Lesser_Antilles_2"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Lesser Antilles</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Haiti_3"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Haiti</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Cuba_2"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Cuba</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#United_States_3"><span class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">United States</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Retirement"><span class="tocnumber">4.5</span> <span class="toctext">Retirement</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meteorological_history">Meteorological history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Meteorological history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Meteorological_history_of_Hurricane_Matthew" title="Meteorological history of Hurricane Matthew">Meteorological history of Hurricane Matthew</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Matthew_2016_track.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2127" data-file-width="3000" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Matthew_2016_track.png/220px-Matthew_2016_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Matthew_2016_track.png/330px-Matthew_2016_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Matthew_2016_track.png/440px-Matthew_2016_track.png 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Matthew_2016_track.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMap plotting the track and intensity of the storm, according to the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale">Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>A vigorous <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> moved off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> on September 22 and moved rapidly across the Atlantic, being monitored by the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> (NHC) for possible <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclogenesis" title="Tropical cyclogenesis">tropical cyclogenesis</a>. Despite possessing tropical-storm winds as it approached the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> on September 27, the wave could not initially be classified as a tropical cyclone, as reconnaissance aircraft could not find a closed center. However, by 12:00\xc2\xa0UTC on September 28, the wave developed a closed circulation while located near <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, hence becoming a tropical storm, and was assigned the name <i>Matthew</i>. Continuing westward under the influence of a mid-level ridge, the storm steadily intensified to attain hurricane intensity by 18:00\xc2\xa0UTC on September\xc2\xa029. The effects of southwesterly wind shear unexpectedly abated late that day, and Matthew began a period of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Explosive_intensification" title="Explosive intensification">explosive intensification</a>; during a 24-hour period beginning at 00:00\xc2\xa0UTC on September\xc2\xa030, the cyclone\'s maximum winds more than doubled, from 80\xc2\xa0mph (130\xc2\xa0km/h) to 165\xc2\xa0mph (270\xc2\xa0km/h), making Matthew a Category 5 hurricane,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1">[1]</a></sup> the first since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Felix" title="Hurricane Felix">Hurricane Felix</a> in 2007;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> the rate of intensification has only been exceeded a few times in the Atlantic since records began. Due to <a href="/wiki/Upwelling" title="Upwelling">upwelling</a> of cooler waters, Matthew weakened to a Category\xc2\xa04 hurricane later on October\xc2\xa01, before attaining a secondary peak intensity with winds of 155\xc2\xa0mph (250\xc2\xa0km/h) late on October 2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1">[1]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Slowly rounding the ridge, Matthew fluctuated in intensity within the Category 4 range from October\xc2\xa01\xe2\x80\x935. Intensification resumed again late on October 3 and culminated when Matthew made landfall near <a href="/wiki/Les_Anglais" title="Les Anglais">Les Anglais</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, around 11:00 UTC on October 4 with winds of 150\xc2\xa0mph (240\xc2\xa0km/h) and a pressure of 934 millibars (27.6\xc2\xa0inHg), making it the strongest to hit Haiti since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Cleo" title="Hurricane Cleo">Hurricane Cleo</a> in 1964. Continuing northward, the hurricane struck <a href="/wiki/Mais%C3%AD" title="Mais\xc3\xad">Mais\xc3\xad</a> in Cuba early on October\xc2\xa05 as a slightly weaker storm. Cuba\'s and Haiti\'s mountainous terrain weakened Matthew to Category 3 status, as it began to accelerate northwestwards through <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">the Bahamas</a>. Restrengthening occurred as Matthew\'s circulation became better organized, with the storm becoming a Category\xc2\xa04 hurricane again while passing <a href="/wiki/Freeport,_Bahamas" title="Freeport, Bahamas">Freeport</a>. However, Matthew began to weaken again as an <a href="/wiki/Eyewall_replacement_cycle" title="Eyewall replacement cycle">eyewall replacement cycle</a> took place. The storm significantly weakened while closely paralleling the coasts of Florida and Georgia, with the northwestern portion of the outer eyewall coming ashore in Florida while the system was a Category\xc2\xa03 hurricane (with the strongest winds remaining just offshore). Matthew weakened to a Category\xc2\xa02 hurricane late on October\xc2\xa07 and then to a Category\xc2\xa01 hurricane by 12:00\xc2\xa0UTC on October\xc2\xa08.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1">[1]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Matthew,_seen_from_the_ISS.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="506" data-file-width="900" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Hurricane_Matthew%2C_seen_from_the_ISS.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Matthew%2C_seen_from_the_ISS.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Hurricane_Matthew%2C_seen_from_the_ISS.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Matthew%2C_seen_from_the_ISS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Hurricane_Matthew%2C_seen_from_the_ISS.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Matthew%2C_seen_from_the_ISS.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Matthew,_seen_from_the_ISS.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe eye of Hurricane Matthew seen from the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> on October 3.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Around 15:00\xc2\xa0UTC on October\xc2\xa08, the hurricane made landfall at <a href="/wiki/Cape_Romain_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Cape Romain National Wildlife Refuge">Cape Romain National Wildlife Refuge</a>, near <a href="/wiki/McClellanville,_South_Carolina" title="McClellanville, South Carolina">McClellanville, South Carolina</a>, with winds of 85\xc2\xa0mph (140\xc2\xa0km/h) and a central pressure of 963\xc2\xa0mbar (28.4\xc2\xa0inHg), which made it the strongest to strike the United States in terms of pressure since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Isaac_(2012)" title="Hurricane Isaac (2012)">Hurricane Isaac</a> in 2012, and the first hurricane to make landfall north of Florida in October since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hazel" title="Hurricane Hazel">Hurricane Hazel</a> in 1954.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[nb 1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1">[1]</a></sup> Convection became displaced from the center as Matthew pulled away from land due to increasing wind shear, with the NHC declaring the system an <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclone</a> about 200\xc2\xa0mi (320\xc2\xa0km) east of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Hatteras,_North_Carolina" title="Cape Hatteras, North Carolina">Cape Hatteras, North Carolina</a>, on October\xc2\xa09. The remnants persisted for another day before they were absorbed by a <a href="/wiki/Cold_front" title="Cold front">cold front</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1">[1]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Records">Records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Matthew set several records during its long and destructive journey. Matthew intensified into a Category\xc2\xa05 hurricane at a <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitude</a> of 13.4\xc2\xa0degrees north, breaking the record set by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ivan" title="Hurricane Ivan">Hurricane Ivan</a> in 2004, which had reached that intensity at a latitude of 13.7\xc2\xa0degrees north.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_1-6"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1">[1]</a></sup> Matthew also maintained at least Category\xc2\xa04 status for the longest duration on record for the month of October, according to Phil Klotzbach of <a href="/wiki/Colorado_State_University" title="Colorado State University">Colorado State University</a>, doing so for roughly 5 days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Preparations">Preparations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Preparations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Matthew_2016-09-28_1430Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1175" data-file-width="900" height="261" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Matthew_2016-09-28_1430Z.jpg/200px-Matthew_2016-09-28_1430Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Matthew_2016-09-28_1430Z.jpg/300px-Matthew_2016-09-28_1430Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Matthew_2016-09-28_1430Z.jpg/400px-Matthew_2016-09-28_1430Z.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Matthew_2016-09-28_1430Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nTropical Storm Matthew over the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>, shortly after formation on September 28</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lesser_Antilles_and_South_America">Lesser Antilles and South America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Lesser Antilles and South America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On September\xc2\xa027, prior to Matthew becoming a tropical cyclone, <a href="/wiki/LIAT" title="LIAT">LIAT</a> began cancelling flights across the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a> in anticipation of squally weather.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup> Schools and businesses were closed for the duration of Matthew\'s passage on September\xc2\xa027 and 28 on <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[7]</a></sup> St. Vincent and St. Lucia; schools in Dominica suspended classes until October\xc2\xa03.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JOSep30_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-JOSep30-9">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NNSep29_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-NNSep29-10">[9]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hewanorra_International_Airport" title="Hewanorra International Airport">Hewanorra International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_F._L._Charles_Airport" title="George F. L. Charles Airport">George F. L. Charles Airport</a> on St. Lucia were closed on September\xc2\xa028.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NNSep29_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-NNSep29-10">[9]</a></sup> Six shelters were opened across the island; 133\xc2\xa0sought refuge in them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SLTSep30_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-SLTSep30-11">[10]</a></sup> Upon the formation of Matthew as a tropical cyclone on September\xc2\xa028, governments across the Windward Islands issued <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_storm_warning" title="Tropical storm warning">tropical storm warnings</a> in anticipation of <a href="/wiki/Gale" title="Gale">gale</a>-force winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Matthew_October_2,_2016,_rainfall_forecast_for_Caribbean.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1995" data-file-width="2048" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Hurricane_Matthew_October_2%2C_2016%2C_rainfall_forecast_for_Caribbean.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Matthew_October_2%2C_2016%2C_rainfall_forecast_for_Caribbean.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Hurricane_Matthew_October_2%2C_2016%2C_rainfall_forecast_for_Caribbean.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Matthew_October_2%2C_2016%2C_rainfall_forecast_for_Caribbean.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Hurricane_Matthew_October_2%2C_2016%2C_rainfall_forecast_for_Caribbean.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Matthew_October_2%2C_2016%2C_rainfall_forecast_for_Caribbean.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Matthew_October_2,_2016,_rainfall_forecast_for_Caribbean.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA map of forecast rainfall totals from Hurricane Matthew for the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Antilles" title="Greater Antilles">Greater Antilles</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">the Bahamas</a>. Peak accumulations in excess of 30\xc2\xa0in (760\xc2\xa0mm) were expected along the southern coast of <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Tiburon_Peninsula" title="Tiburon Peninsula">Tiburon Peninsula</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The storm\'s unusual south track prompted the issuance of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_storm_watch" title="Tropical storm watch">tropical storm watches</a> on September\xc2\xa028 for <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Cura\xc3\xa7ao">Cura\xc3\xa7ao</a>, and the northern coast of <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> from the Colombia\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> border to <a href="/wiki/Riohacha" title="Riohacha">Riohacha</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> North Atlantic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_South_America_tropical_cyclones" title="List of South America tropical cyclones">hurricanes affecting South America</a> are uncommon. The watch in Colombia was later upgraded to a warning on September\xc2\xa030 as Matthew continued on a west-southwest track near the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup> Residents across the <a href="/wiki/ABC_islands_(Lesser_Antilles)" title="ABC islands (Lesser Antilles)">ABC Islands</a> were advised to board their homes and stock up on supplies, leading to long lines at supermarkets and gas stations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FredAPSep30_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FredAPSep30-16">[15]</a></sup> Cura\xc3\xa7ao\'s government postponed the <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_general_election,_2016" title="Cura\xc3\xa7ao general election, 2016">2016 general election</a> until October\xc2\xa05.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOSSep30_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOSSep30-17">[16]</a></sup> Government offices in Aruba closed for September\xc2\xa030.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FredAPSep30_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-FredAPSep30-16">[15]</a></sup> A local sporting event, the Kingdom Tournament, was canceled in Aruba.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOSSep30_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-NOSSep30-17">[16]</a></sup> Schools across the <a href="/wiki/Guajira_Peninsula" title="Guajira Peninsula">Guajira Peninsula</a> of <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> suspended activities for September\xc2\xa030.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ETSep30_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-ETSep30-18">[17]</a></sup> Officials opened shelters and closed beaches across the peninsula.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EHOct1_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-EHOct1-19">[18]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jamaica">Jamaica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Jamaica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>With Matthew posing a significant threat to <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, emergency officials ordered all fishermen on the nation\'s cays and banks to evacuate to the mainland on September\xc2\xa029. The following day, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Jamaica" title="Prime Minister of Jamaica">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Holness" title="Andrew Holness">Andrew Holness</a> held an emergency meeting regarding the hurricane and placed the government on high alert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_watch" title="Hurricane watch">hurricane watch</a> was issued for the country on September\xc2\xa030,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PA11_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-PA11-21">[20]</a></sup> and later upgraded to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_warning" title="Hurricane warning">warning</a> on October\xc2\xa01.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PA15_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-PA15-22">[21]</a></sup> Officials in <a href="/wiki/Trelawny_Parish" title="Trelawny Parish">Trelawny Parish</a> placed 60\xc2\xa0shelters on stand-by on October\xc2\xa02.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> Supermarkets were overwhelmed with residents stocking up on supplies, and many reported empty shelves and low supplies of bread, kerosene, and candles. Many people boarded up their homes and protected their property with sand bags. One hundred female prisoners were relocated from a facility in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Catherine_Parish" title="St. Catherine Parish">St. Catherine Parish</a> to another in <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Jamaica" title="Kingston, Jamaica">Kingston</a>. Toll fees along <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Highway_2000,_Jamaica" title="Highway 2000, Jamaica">Highway 2000</a> were to be waived during the hours before Matthew\'s arrival. Service at both <a href="/wiki/Norman_Manley_International_Airport" title="Norman Manley International Airport">Norman Manley International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sangster_International_Airport" title="Sangster International Airport">Sangster International Airport</a> was scheduled to be suspended during the evening of October\xc2\xa02 or by the morning of October\xc2\xa03.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Jamaica_Urban_Transit_Company" title="Jamaica Urban Transit Company">Jamaica Urban Transit Company</a> scheduled to suspend services beginning at 6:00\xc2\xa0p.m. local time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jamaica_Public_Service&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jamaica Public Service (page does not exist)">Jamaica Public Service</a> informed residents that the power grid might be shut off during the storm if conditions became severe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> Members of the <a href="/wiki/Jamaica_Defence_Force" title="Jamaica Defence Force">Jamaica Defence Force</a> were deployed nationwide in advance of the hurricane in order to more swiftly deal with its aftermath.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Schools and government offices suspended operations starting on October\xc2\xa03.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JOOct3_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-JOOct3-28">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> A total of 900\xc2\xa0shelters opened across Jamaica and the Urban Transit Company provided buses to evacuate people from Kingston to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Arena_(Jamaica)" title="National Arena (Jamaica)">National Arena</a>. Local Minister Desmond McKenzie warned that the infrastructure of Kingston would be unable to handle the magnitude of rainfall expected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JOOct3_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-JOOct3-28">[27]</a></sup> Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Holness" title="Andrew Holness">Andrew Holness</a> warned residents that Matthew could be more severe than <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gilbert" title="Hurricane Gilbert">Hurricane Gilbert</a> which devastated the nation in 1988.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Haiti">Haiti</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Haiti">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n<div class="PopUpMediaTransform" id="mwe_player_0" style="width:220px;" videopayload=\'&lt;div class="mediaContainer" style="width:854px"&gt;&lt;video class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GPM_Captures_Hurricane_Matthew_Before_Haiti_Landfall.webm" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe animation shows Hurricane Matthew from September\xc2\xa028 to October\xc2\xa02, and 3-dimensional radar data from GPM\'s DPR instrument.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Though forecast to pass over Jamaica at the time, the large extent of tropical storm-force winds prompted the issuance of a tropical storm watch for <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Tiburon_Peninsula" title="Tiburon Peninsula">Tiburon Peninsula</a> toward the border with the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PA11_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-PA11-21">[20]</a></sup> Following an eastward shift in Matthew\'s predicted track, a hurricane watch was issued for much of Haiti on October\xc2\xa01, encompassing areas from <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B4le-Saint-Nicolas" title="M\xc3\xb4le-Saint-Nicolas">M\xc3\xb4le-Saint-Nicolas</a> south to the Dominican Republic border;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PA14_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-PA14-31">[30]</a></sup> this was upgraded to a warning just hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PA15_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-PA15-22">[21]</a></sup> The warning eventually encompassed the entire country by the afternoon of October\xc2\xa02.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PA17_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-PA17-32">[31]</a></sup> Residents on outlying islands of Haiti were evacuated to the mainland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCOct2_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBCOct2-33">[32]</a></sup> Life-threatening rainfall was forecast to affect much of the nation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> with accumulations averaging 15 to 25\xc2\xa0in (38 to 64\xc2\xa0cm) along the southern coast with isolated peaks up to 40\xc2\xa0in (100\xc2\xa0cm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> Although government officials held meetings on storm preparation, <a href="/wiki/Radio_France_Internationale" title="Radio France Internationale">Radio France Internationale</a> reported that Haiti does not have the logistical capability to handle a large-scale disaster. Only 576 shelters, with a collective capacity of 90,000\xc2\xa0people, were listed for all of southern Haiti.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Migration" title="International Organization for Migration">International Organization for Migration</a>, 55,107\xc2\xa0<a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_person" title="Internally displaced person">internally displaced persons</a> remained in camps or hosting sites without adequate protection from the hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Provisional President of Haiti <a href="/wiki/Jocelerme_Privert" title="Jocelerme Privert">Jocelerme Privert</a> addressed the nation on October\xc2\xa02, urging those living along the coast and in poorly constructed homes to evacuate and comply with authorities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HLOct2_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-HLOct2-38">[37]</a></sup> Despite pleas from officials, many residents refused to leave their homes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> Schools were closed for October\xc2\xa03\xe2\x80\x934, though government offices remained open.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HLOct2_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-HLOct2-38">[37]</a></sup> Nationwide, a total of 1,300\xc2\xa0shelters were readied with a total capacity of 390,000\xc2\xa0people. More than 18,000\xc2\xa0volunteers and members of the Red Cross, community intervention teams, municipal committees, and local emergency services were readied to assist residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> At least 500\xc2\xa0people were evacuated from <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A9r%C3%A9mie" title="J\xc3\xa9r\xc3\xa9mie">J\xc3\xa9r\xc3\xa9mie</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RCNOct3_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-RCNOct3-41">[40]</a></sup> Although civil protection officials took to the streets to warn people, many residents were unaware that Matthew was even approaching the country a day before its expected landfall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TWCOct3_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-TWCOct3-42">[41]</a></sup> Evacuations continued through the hurricane\'s landfall with the total number of people in shelters reaching 9,280 by 2:00\xc2\xa0a.m. local time on October\xc2\xa04.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On October 5, the Electoral Provisional Council postponed the <a href="/wiki/Haitian_presidential_election,_November_2016" title="Haitian presidential election, November 2016">presidential election</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Haitian_parliamentary_election,_2015%E2%80%9316" title="Haitian parliamentary election, 2015\xe2\x80\x9316">second round of the legislative elections</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Senate_election,_2016%E2%80%9317" title="Haitian Senate election, 2016\xe2\x80\x9317">first round of the Senate elections</a> until November 20.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dominican_Republic">Dominican Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Dominican Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On the morning of October\xc2\xa02, a tropical storm warning was raised for the southern coast of the Dominican Republic from <a href="/wiki/Barahona,_Dominican_Republic" title="Barahona, Dominican Republic">Barahona</a> west to the Haitian border, and a tropical storm watch was issued for the northern coast from <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Plata,_Dominican_Republic" title="Puerto Plata, Dominican Republic">Puerto Plata</a> west to the Haitian border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PA16a_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-PA16a-45">[44]</a></sup> At least 8,500\xc2\xa0people were evacuated in southwestern areas of the country by the morning of October\xc2\xa03.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RCNOct3_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-RCNOct3-41">[40]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuba_and_the_Bahamas">Cuba and the Bahamas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Cuba and the Bahamas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Matthew_en_route_to_Florida.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="720" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Hurricane_Matthew_en_route_to_Florida.gif/220px-Hurricane_Matthew_en_route_to_Florida.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Hurricane_Matthew_en_route_to_Florida.gif/330px-Hurricane_Matthew_en_route_to_Florida.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Hurricane_Matthew_en_route_to_Florida.gif/440px-Hurricane_Matthew_en_route_to_Florida.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Matthew_en_route_to_Florida.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nAnimation of Hurricane Matthew passing through the Bahamas on October\xc2\xa05\xe2\x80\x936</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The Meteorological Service of Cuba raised hurricane watches for all of southeastern <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> on October\xc2\xa01, encompassing the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Camag%C3%BCey_Province" title="Camag\xc3\xbcey Province">Camag\xc3\xbcey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Las_Tunas_Province" title="Las Tunas Province">Las Tunas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Granma_Province" title="Granma Province">Granma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holgu%C3%ADn_Province" title="Holgu\xc3\xadn Province">Holgu\xc3\xadn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Cuba_Province" title="Santiago de Cuba Province">Santiago de Cuba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guant%C3%A1namo_Province" title="Guant\xc3\xa1namo Province">Guant\xc3\xa1namo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PA15_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-PA15-22">[21]</a></sup> This was subsequently upgraded to a warning on October\xc2\xa02 for all provinces except Camag\xc3\xbcey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PA17_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-PA17-32">[31]</a></sup> Non-essential personnel in the United States\' <a href="/wiki/Guantanamo_Bay_Naval_Base" title="Guantanamo Bay Naval Base">Guantanamo Bay Naval Base</a> began evacuations that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCOct2_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBCOct2-33">[32]</a></sup> Evacuations of more than 1\xc2\xa0million people across Cuba started that morning, including 252,000 in Santiago de Cuba, and 230,000 from Las Tunas with priority placed on those along the coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RROct2_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-RROct2-46">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MilOct2_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-MilOct2-47">[46]</a></sup> Across Santiago de Cuba, which suffered extensive damage from <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sandy" title="Hurricane Sandy">Hurricane Sandy</a> in 2012, 218\xc2\xa0shelters were opened and officials placed extra attention on Socapa, Caracoles, and Cayo Granma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RROct2_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-RROct2-46">[45]</a></sup> Emergency personnel, primarily doctors, were dispatched to high-risk areas and supplies were stockpiled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MilOct2_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-MilOct2-47">[46]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The Government of the Bahamas began issuing hurricane watches on October\xc2\xa02 for southeastern islands as well as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos" title="Turks and Caicos">Turks and Caicos</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PA17_32-2"><a href="#cite_note-PA17-32">[31]</a></sup> Flights across southern islands were cancelled and schools suspended operations beginning the following day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Richard_Knabb_discussing_Hurricane_Matthew_October_6,_2016.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Richard_Knabb_discussing_Hurricane_Matthew_October_6%2C_2016.jpg/220px-Richard_Knabb_discussing_Hurricane_Matthew_October_6%2C_2016.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Richard_Knabb_discussing_Hurricane_Matthew_October_6%2C_2016.jpg/330px-Richard_Knabb_discussing_Hurricane_Matthew_October_6%2C_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Richard_Knabb_discussing_Hurricane_Matthew_October_6%2C_2016.jpg/440px-Richard_Knabb_discussing_Hurricane_Matthew_October_6%2C_2016.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Richard_Knabb_discussing_Hurricane_Matthew_October_6,_2016.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nNational Hurricane Center Director <a href="/wiki/Richard_Knabb" title="Richard Knabb">Richard Knabb</a> <i>(pictured)</i> regularly filmed briefings on the forecast and expected impacts of Hurricane Matthew in the United States.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>On October\xc2\xa03, the governors of <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> declared a <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> The next day, <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a> governor <a href="/wiki/Nikki_Haley" title="Nikki Haley">Nikki Haley</a> ordered an evacuation for those residents living within one hundred miles (160\xc2\xa0km) of the coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Interstate_26_in_South_Carolina" title="Interstate 26 in South Carolina">Interstate 26 in South Carolina</a> eastbound between the coast and <a href="/wiki/Columbia,_South_Carolina" title="Columbia, South Carolina">Columbia</a> was <a href="/wiki/Contraflow_lane_reversal" title="Contraflow lane reversal">reversed</a> on Wednesday to facilitate movement away from the <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_Lowcountry" title="South Carolina Lowcountry">Lowcountry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="Charleston, South Carolina">Charleston</a> areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABC26_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-ABC26-52">[51]</a></sup> Evacuations of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Lookout_National_Seashore" title="Cape Lookout National Seashore">Cape Lookout National Seashore</a> in North Carolina began this day as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> By October\xc2\xa04, North Carolina Governor <a href="/wiki/Pat_McCrory" title="Pat McCrory">Pat McCrory</a> had ordered that evacuation be mandatory. A state of emergency was also declared for 13\xc2\xa0counties in eastern <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On October\xc2\xa05, <a href="/wiki/Port_Canaveral" title="Port Canaveral">Port Canaveral</a> was closed by the U.S. Coast Guard, the first closure since 2004. Eight cruise ships and four cargo ships were scheduled to visit the port between October\xc2\xa05\xe2\x80\x939.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FT:_Port_closure_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-FT:_Port_closure-55">[54]</a></sup> On Cape Canaveral, home to both civilian and military spaceflight facilities, no rockets or spacecraft were in vulnerable positions; at the time of Matthew\'s approach, the next launch was scheduled for November\xc2\xa04.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FT:_Cape_Canaveral_preparations_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FT:_Cape_Canaveral_preparations-56">[55]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">Kennedy Space Center</a> began preparations of the facilities on October\xc2\xa05. Older buildings at the KSC were designed to withstand winds of 105\xe2\x80\x93125\xc2\xa0mph (170\xe2\x80\x93200\xc2\xa0km/h); buildings constructed after 1992, when Category\xc2\xa05 <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Andrew" title="Hurricane Andrew">Hurricane Andrew</a> struck the Miami area, are built to withstand 130\xc2\xa0mph (210\xc2\xa0km/h) winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AT:_KSC_threat_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-AT:_KSC_threat-57">[56]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Cape_Canaveral_Air_Force_Station" title="Cape Canaveral Air Force Station">Cape Canaveral Air Force Station</a>, the U.S. Air Force\'s <a href="/wiki/45th_Space_Wing" title="45th Space Wing">45th Space Wing</a> began disconnecting electric power to non-essential facilities on October\xc2\xa04.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FT:_Cape_Canaveral_preparations_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-FT:_Cape_Canaveral_preparations-56">[55]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Matthew_2016-10-06_1745Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1600" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Matthew_2016-10-06_1745Z.jpg/220px-Matthew_2016-10-06_1745Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Matthew_2016-10-06_1745Z.jpg/330px-Matthew_2016-10-06_1745Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Matthew_2016-10-06_1745Z.jpg/440px-Matthew_2016-10-06_1745Z.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Matthew_2016-10-06_1745Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nHurricane Matthew nearing <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> on October\xc2\xa06</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>For the fourth time in its 45-year history, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_World_Resort" title="Walt Disney World Resort">Walt Disney World Resort</a> closes. Its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theme_park" title="Theme park">theme parks</a> are <a href="/wiki/Magic_Kingdom" title="Magic Kingdom">Magic Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Epcot" title="Epcot">Epcot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disney%27s_Hollywood_Studios" title="Disney\'s Hollywood Studios">Disney\'s Hollywood Studios</a> and <a href="/wiki/Disney%27s_Animal_Kingdom" title="Disney\'s Animal Kingdom">Disney\'s Animal Kingdom</a> <a href="/wiki/Water_park" title="Water park">water parks</a> are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blizzard_Beach" title="Blizzard Beach">Blizzard Beach</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Typhoon_Lagoon" title="Typhoon Lagoon">Typhoon Lagoon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Disney_Springs" title="Disney Springs">Disney Springs</a> were closed at 5:00\xc2\xa0p.m. Eastern Time on October 6 and did not open on October\xc2\xa07.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> This was the first time since 2004 that the parks have closed, all instances due to hurricanes. Other Orlando-area theme parks, including <a href="/wiki/Universal_Orlando" title="Universal Orlando">Universal Orlando</a> resort and <a href="/wiki/SeaWorld_Orlando" title="SeaWorld Orlando">SeaWorld Orlando</a>, also closed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference" title="Southeastern Conference">Southeastern Conference</a> football matchup between <a href="/wiki/LSU_Tigers_football" title="LSU Tigers football">LSU</a> and <a href="/wiki/Florida_Gators_football" title="Florida Gators football">Florida</a>, scheduled for October 8 in Gainesville, was cancelled. The hurricane washed out <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> racing at <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Motor_Speedway" title="Charlotte Motor Speedway">Charlotte Motor Speedway</a> on October 7 and 8, with the <a href="/wiki/Drive_for_the_Cure_300" title="Drive for the Cure 300">Drive for the Cure 300</a> race in the <a href="/wiki/Xfinity_Series" title="Xfinity Series">Xfinity Series</a> originally scheduled for October 7 and the <a href="/wiki/2016_Bank_of_America_500" title="2016 Bank of America 500">Bank of America 500</a> race in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sprint_Cup_Series" title="Sprint Cup Series">Sprint Cup Series</a> originally scheduled for October 8 both postponed until October 9.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On October\xc2\xa06, U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> declared a federal <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a> for Florida,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup> later extending to include Georgia and South Carolina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> Florida\'s governor <a href="/wiki/Rick_Scott" title="Rick Scott">Rick Scott</a> urged over 1.5 million people to evacuate,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> with Hurricane Matthew expected to make landfall by the evening of that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> Several <a href="/wiki/News_presenter" title="News presenter">news anchors</a> also issued dire warnings urging Floridians to evacuate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FoxNewsWarning_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FoxNewsWarning-66">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup></p>\n<p>That same day, Georgia governor <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Deal" title="Nathan Deal">Nathan Deal</a> ordered a mandatory evacuation for all areas of the state east of <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Georgia" title="Interstate 95 in Georgia">Interstate 95</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Georgia_Department_of_Public_Safety" title="Georgia Department of Public Safety">Georgia Department of Public Safety</a> reversed the eastbound lanes on a portion of <a href="/wiki/Interstate_16" title="Interstate 16">Interstate 16</a> effective until the following day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Online_response">Online response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Online response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On October\xc2\xa06, the <a href="/wiki/Conservatism_in_the_United_States" title="Conservatism in the United States">conservative</a> <a href="/wiki/News_aggregator" title="News aggregator">news aggregator</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Drudge_Report" title="Drudge Report">Drudge Report</a></i>\xe2\x80\x94run by <a href="/wiki/Matt_Drudge" title="Matt Drudge">Matt Drudge</a>\xe2\x80\x94headlined a five-word comment on Matthew: "Storm Fizzle? Matthew Looks Ragged!" which linked to a <i>Miami Herald</i> article.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TWP_Drudge_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-TWP_Drudge-70">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Drudge6th_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Drudge6th-71">[70]</a></sup> Drudge later used Twitter to claim that the National Hurricane Center was lying to the public about the intensity of the storm, stating that measurements from Nassau, Bahamas, did not match the 165\xc2\xa0mph (270\xc2\xa0km/h) gusts listed in public advisories. The tweets implied that the hurricane was not as dangerous as it seemed and that politicians were trying to "<a href="/wiki/Global_warming_conspiracy_theory" title="Global warming conspiracy theory">blame mankind</a>,"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPR_Drudge_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-NPR_Drudge-72">[71]</a></sup> referring to a blog posting about Hillary Clinton.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPR_Drudge_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-NPR_Drudge-72">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HillaryBlog_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-HillaryBlog-73">[72]</a></sup> This came on the heels of radio talk show host <a href="/wiki/Rush_Limbaugh" title="Rush Limbaugh">Rush Limbaugh</a>\'s claims of the conspiracy to "sell" climate change.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> The claims of conspiracy were posted as Matthew posed a dire threat to Florida\'s east coast and when residents across the state were being urged to evacuate immediately.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> Drudge\'s commentary was quickly met with sharp condemnation and criticism from meteorologists and public officials. Democratic <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">Representative</a> <a href="/wiki/Keith_Ellison" title="Keith Ellison">Keith Ellison</a> called the comments "irresponsible" and urged people to "not listen to this man."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPR_Drudge_72-2"><a href="#cite_note-NPR_Drudge-72">[71]</a></sup> Jason Samenow of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> described it as an "incredible and offensive accusation", and stated that it "may have introduced enough doubt to lead [residents] into a decision they will regret."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TWP_Drudge_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-TWP_Drudge-70">[69]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">Impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table align="right" class="wikitable sortable">\n<caption><b>Deaths and damage by class="table-na" data-sort-value="" style="background: #ececec; color: #2C2C2C; vertical-align: middle; font-size: smaller; text-align: center;">N/A</td>\n<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_1-7"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DR_Deaths_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-DR_Deaths-79">[78]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a></td>\n<td>546</td>\n<td>546</td>\n<td>0</td>\n<td>128</td>\n<td><span class="sortkey" id="cite_ref-NG.com_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-NG.com-80">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WFP_Oct11_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-WFP_Oct11-81">[80]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent<br/>\nand the Grenadines</a></td>\n<td>1</td>\n<td>1</td>\n<td>0</td>\n<td>0</td>\n<td class="table-na" data-sort-value="" style="background: #ececec; color: #2C2C2C; vertical-align: middle; font-size: smaller; States</a></td>\n<td>47</td>\n<td>34</td>\n<td>13</td>\n<td>0</td>\n<td><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7010100000000000000\xe2\x99\xa0</span>$10\xc2\xa0billion</td>\n<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_1-10"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1">[1]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr class="sortbottom">\n<th>Totals:</th>\n<th><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7002603000000000000\xe2\x99\xa0</span>603</th>\n<th>586</th>\n<th>17</th>\n<th>128</th>\n<th><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7010150880000000000\xe2\x99\xa0</span>$15.1\xc2\xa0billion</th>\n<th></th>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lesser_Antilles">Lesser Antilles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Lesser Antilles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_(Antilles)" title="Saint Vincent (Antilles)">St. Vincent</a> heavy rains caused landslides and flooding across the island. One person was killed in the town of Layou when a boulder broke loose and crushed him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JOSep30_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-JOSep30-9">[8]</a></sup> In nearby Buccament Bay, a river overtopped its banks, prompting at least 25\xc2\xa0people to evacuate to emergency shelters. The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hermitage_River&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hermitage River (page does not exist)">Hermitage River</a> rose by at least 3.6\xc2\xa0ft (1.1\xc2\xa0m) in one hour, and as a precautionary measure, the Central Water and Sewage Authority shut off all water service. Flooding also took place in Vermont, South Rivers, sections of Kingstown, Campden Park, Arnos Vale, and Langley Park. Debris deposited by flooded rivers rendered many roads impassable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NNSep29_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-NNSep29-10">[9]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Strong winds in excess of 60\xc2\xa0mph (97\xc2\xa0km/h) downed many trees and power lines on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Lucia" title="St. Lucia">St. Lucia</a>, leaving roughly 70\xc2\xa0percent of the island without power. Landslides and flooding, the result of more than 10\xc2\xa0in (250\xc2\xa0mm) of rain accompanying the storm, damaged many homes and roads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JOSep30_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-JOSep30-9">[8]</a></sup> Rainfall at Hewanorra International Airport amounted to 13.19\xc2\xa0in (335\xc2\xa0mm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TWCSep29_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-TWCSep29-82">[81]</a></sup> The nation\'s banana crop suffered significant damage; 85\xc2\xa0percent of farms reported losses. Two homes were destroyed, one in Bisee, and one in Gros Islet; several others were damaged. Roads in Castries, Gros-Islet, Dennery, and Soufriere became impassible from debris or landslides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SLTSep30_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-SLTSep30-11">[10]</a></sup> Some damage was also reported on <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>, temporarily leaving many people without water and electricity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JOSep30_9-4"><a href="#cite_note-JOSep30-9">[8]</a></sup> Heavy rainfall in Grenada disrupted the water supply in multiple communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> strong winds, which gusted up to 89\xc2\xa0mph (143\xc2\xa0km/h) in <a href="/wiki/Saint-Pierre,_Martinique" title="Saint-Pierre, Martinique">Saint-Pierre</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TWCSep29_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-TWCSep29-82">[81]</a></sup> wreaked havoc on the power grid; roughly 55,000\xc2\xa0people lost electricity. Numerous trees downed by the winds blocked roadways while heavy rains led to flooding. The main road from <a href="/wiki/Fort-de-France" title="Fort-de-France">Fort-de-France</a> to southern towns was rendered impassable during the storm. Approximately 4,000\xc2\xa0people lost their water supply. Three people sustained minor injuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LCISep30_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-LCISep30-84">[83]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ABC_Islands_and_South_America">ABC Islands and South America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: ABC Islands and South America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The effects of Matthew across the ABC Islands were relatively limited despite its proximity. Some street flooding occurred on Aruba and Cura\xc3\xa7ao. Heavy winds were also experienced. There was some damage to cars after street flooding occurred. Outdoor bars and restaurants were damaged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FredAPSep30_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-FredAPSep30-16">[15]</a></sup> The Guajira Peninsula of Colombia saw its first heavy rain event in three years, leading to widespread flash flooding. One person drowned in a swollen river in <a href="/wiki/Uribia,_La_Guajira" title="Uribia, La Guajira">Uribia</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EHOct1_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-EHOct1-19">[18]</a></sup> 1.29\xc2\xa0in (32.8\xc2\xa0mm) of rain fell in 30\xc2\xa0minutes in the town.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> Rainfall in <a href="/wiki/Cartagena,_Colombia" title="Cartagena, Colombia">Cartagena</a> reached 8.7\xc2\xa0in (222\xc2\xa0mm) during a 24-hour span and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Marta" title="Santa Marta">Santa Marta</a> saw 5.5\xc2\xa0in (140\xc2\xa0mm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ECOct3_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-ECOct3-86">[85]</a></sup> Along coastal areas of the peninsula, large swells damaged buildings, prompting the evacuation of 380\xc2\xa0people in <a href="/wiki/Manaure,_La_Guajira" title="Manaure, La Guajira">Manaure</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ETSep30_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-ETSep30-18">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EHOct1_19-3"><a href="#cite_note-EHOct1-19">[18]</a></sup> Roughly 70\xc2\xa0percent of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tucurinca&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tucurinca (page does not exist)">Tucurinca</a> flooded when the <a href="/wiki/Magdalena_River" title="Magdalena River">Magdalena River</a> overtopped its banks; a nearby bridge collapsed, isolating some communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> Approximately 73,000\xc2\xa0people were affected by the floods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ECOct3_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-ECOct3-86">[85]</a></sup> The dangerous conditions produced by Matthew prevented thousands of people from voting in a <a href="/wiki/Colombian_peace_agreement_referendum,_2016" title="Colombian peace agreement referendum, 2016">peace agreement referendum</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LVOct2_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-LVOct2-88">[87]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jamaica_2">Jamaica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Jamaica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">\n<tr>\n<td class="mbox-image">\n<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>\n</td>\n<td class="mbox-text">\n<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small><i>(September 2017)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Jamaica suffered relatively minor effects, characteristic of tropical storm conditions. Along the coast, rip currents and beach erosion was reported, with additional flooding due to rainfall occurring. Strong wind gusts tore at the island\'s vegetation, causing minor damage.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Haiti_2">Haiti</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Haiti">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Matthew_in_Haiti" title="Effects of Hurricane Matthew in Haiti">Effects of Hurricane Matthew in Haiti</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Matthew_2016-10-03_1515Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1100" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Matthew_2016-10-03_1515Z.jpg/220px-Matthew_2016-10-03_1515Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Matthew_2016-10-03_1515Z.jpg/330px-Matthew_2016-10-03_1515Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Matthew_2016-10-03_1515Z.jpg/440px-Matthew_2016-10-03_1515Z.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Matthew_2016-10-03_1515Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nHurricane Matthew approaching Jamaica, Haiti and Cuba on October\xc2\xa03</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Large swells reached the outlying Haitian island of <a href="/wiki/%C3%8Ele-%C3%A0-Vache" title="\xc3\x8ele-\xc3\xa0-Vache">\xc3\x8ele-\xc3\xa0-Vache</a> on October\xc2\xa02, prompting the evacuation of 89\xc2\xa0people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> Despite boating bans, many fishermen continued work in rough conditions. Consequently, two fishermen went missing on the morning of October\xc2\xa03: one near <a href="/wiki/Saint-Jean-du-Sud" title="Saint-Jean-du-Sud">Saint-Jean-du-Sud</a> and the other near <a href="/wiki/Aquin" title="Aquin">Aquin</a>; one was later found dead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TWCOct3_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-TWCOct3-42">[41]</a></sup> Antecedent rainfall associated with the outer bands of Matthew triggered flooding in several towns in southern Haiti and the Dominican Republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RCNOct3_41-2"><a href="#cite_note-RCNOct3-41">[40]</a></sup> A person was killed when a tree fell on his home in <a href="/wiki/Port_Salut" title="Port Salut">Port Salut</a>, while a 26-year-old man drowned while trying to rescue a child from a rushing river.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Striking the Tiburon Peninsula as a Category\xc2\xa04 hurricane on the morning of October\xc2\xa04, Matthew was the strongest storm to directly impact Haiti since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Cleo" title="Hurricane Cleo">Hurricane Cleo</a> in 1964. An anemometer at <a href="/wiki/Antoine-Simon_Airport" title="Antoine-Simon Airport">Antoine-Simon Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Les_Cayes" title="Les Cayes">Les Cayes</a>, east of where Matthew made landfall, measured a gust of 107\xc2\xa0mph (172\xc2\xa0km/h) before the station went offline. Gusts in the nation\'s capital city of <a href="/wiki/Port-au-Prince" title="Port-au-Prince">Port-au-Prince</a> reached 60\xc2\xa0mph (97\xc2\xa0km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> Communications with areas in the direct path of Matthew were lost, and tens of thousands of people became isolated as roads and bridges were destroyed. A major bridge connecting parts of <a href="/wiki/Grand%27Anse_(department)" title="Grand\'Anse (department)">Grand\'Anse</a> to the rest of the country collapsed during a flash flood. 80% of <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A9r%C3%A9mie" title="J\xc3\xa9r\xc3\xa9mie">J\xc3\xa9r\xc3\xa9mie</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-92">[91]</a></sup> along the north shore of the Tiburon Peninsula, suffered tremendous damage; homes were flattened and medical facilities suffered major damage. A radio host in Port-au-Prince stated that J\xc3\xa9r\xc3\xa9mie was "pretty much wiped out from the seaboard all the way to the cathedral".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCOct6_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBCOct6-93">[92]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Officially, 546 deaths were attributed to the storm in Haiti,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_1-11"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1">[1]</a></sup> however local governments believed the death toll to be over 1,000; this value may have been overestimated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cedim_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-cedim-94">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters-Matthew.27s_death_toll_hits_1.2C000_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-Matthew.27s_death_toll_hits_1.2C000-96">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haiti_Deaths_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Haiti_Deaths-98">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> According to the nation\'s Civil Protection Directorate, the death toll was 546 as of October\xc2\xa014, with 128\xc2\xa0people missing and 439\xc2\xa0injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NG.com_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-NG.com-80">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WFP_Oct11_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-WFP_Oct11-81">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> This figure was later confirmed by the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_1-12"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1">[1]</a></sup> The government also estimates damages at close to $1.9 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_1-13"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yahoo_10-29-16_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo_10-29-16-101">[100]</a></sup> Approximately 2.1\xc2\xa0million people were affected by the storm, of whom 1.4\xc2\xa0million (12\xc2\xa0percent of Haiti\'s population) were left in need of assistance. Furthermore, roughly 175,000\xc2\xa0people were left homeless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WFP_Oct11_81-2"><a href="#cite_note-WFP_Oct11-81">[80]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dominican_Republic_2">Dominican Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Dominican Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Dominican Republic reported significant rainfall and coastal flooding due to Matthew, an automated weather station in <a href="/wiki/Cabo_Rojo,_Dominican_Republic" title="Cabo Rojo, Dominican Republic">Cabo Rojo, Dominican Republic</a>, measured 8.43\xc2\xa0in (214\xc2\xa0mm) of rain by the afternoon of October\xc2\xa03.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> Four people died in the Dominican Republic after a house collapsed on top of them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DR_Deaths_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-DR_Deaths-79">[78]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuba">Cuba</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Cuba">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table border="1" class="wikitable sortable plainrowheaders" style="font-size: 92%; float:right; href="#cite_note-WMO_2004-109">[108]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:View_of_cliff_erosion_and_wave_size_reduction_the_morning_after_Hurricane_Matthew._(30159059326).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2567" data-file-width="3875" 1.5x,
