2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:View_of_cliff_erosion_and_wave_size_reduction_the_morning_after_Hurricane_Matthew._(30159059326).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nView of cliff <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">erosion</a> a day after Hurricane Matthew hit <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naval_Station_Guantanamo_Bay" title="Naval Station Guantanamo Bay">Naval Station Guantanamo Bay</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Coastal flooding began in Granma Province, Cuba, on October\xc2\xa02, affecting three towns along the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Maestra" title="Sierra Maestra">Sierra Maestras</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RROct2_46-2"><a href="#cite_note-RROct2-46">[45]</a></sup> Hurricane Matthew struck the easternmost province of Cuba during the evening of October\xc2\xa04 as a Category\xc2\xa04, causing tremendous damage. The coastal city of <a href="/wiki/Baracoa" title="Baracoa">Baracoa</a> suffered widespread damage from violent winds, and <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">storm surge</a>, the latter of which gutted countless buildings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup> Despite the severity of damage, no fatalities were reported in the city. A communication tower in Majayara collapsed during the storm and a bridge spanning the <a href="/wiki/Toa_river" title="Toa river">Toa river</a> was destroyed; several communities left isolated as a result.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> Damages in Cuba amounted to $2.58\xc2\xa0billion USD; most of which occurred in the Guant\xc3\xa1namo Province.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_China_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-New_China-104">[103]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Nearly two months later, on November 22, a municipal bridge in the city of <a href="/wiki/Moa,_Cuba" title="Moa, Cuba">Moa</a> that was damaged by Hurricane Matthew collapsed, killing four employees of Canadian mining company <a href="/wiki/Sherritt_International" title="Sherritt International">Sherritt International</a>. The employees were undertaking repairs to restore access between Moa and a mining site.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BNO_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-BNO-78">[77]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bahamas">Bahamas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Bahamas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Experiencing a direct hit from the eyewall of Matthew, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Bahama" title="Grand Bahama">Grand Bahama</a> suffered extensive damage. An estimated 95\xc2\xa0percent of homes in Eight Mile Rock and Holmes Rock sustained severe damage. Numerous trees and power lines were toppled by the storm\'s high winds, rendering roads impassable. Flooding-induced by the backside of the storm affected much of the western half of the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup> Total losses from Matthew in the Bahamas are estimated to be around $600\xc2\xa0million USD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb-76">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_2">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:right; margin:0 0 0.5em 1em; float:right;">\n<caption><b>Deaths and damage by U.S. state</b></caption>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<th scope="col">State</th>\n<th scope="col">Deaths</th>\n<th scope="col">Damage</th>\n<th scope="col">Ref</th>\n</tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td><a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a></td>\n<td>12</td>\n<td>$2.75\xc2\xa0billion</td>\n<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td><a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a></td>\n<td>3</td>\n<td>&gt;$90\xc2\xa0million</td>\n<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td><a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a></td>\n<td>26</td>\n<td>$1.6\xc2\xa0billion</td>\n<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NorthCarolina26deaths_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-NorthCarolina26deaths-116">[115]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td><a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a></td>\n<td>4</td>\n<td>$249.6\xc2\xa0million</td>\n<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<td><a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a></td>\n<td>2</td>\n<td>$58.14\xc2\xa0million</td>\n<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>In total, the storm killed 47 people in the US, including 26 in North Carolina, 12 in Florida, 3 in Georgia, 4 in South Carolina, and 2 in Virginia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_AP_10-15-16_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_AP_10-15-16-119">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Dispatch_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Dispatch-120">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stradling_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stradling-121">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-122">[121]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/National_Centers_for_Environmental_Information" title="National Centers for Environmental Information">National Centers for Environmental Information</a>, damage from Matthew across the United States reached approximately $10\xc2\xa0billion. This ranked it the costliest national disaster in the country for 2016 alongside <a href="/wiki/2016_Louisiana_floods" title="2016 Louisiana floods">record floods in Louisiana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Florida_and_Georgia">Florida and Georgia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Florida and Georgia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>As Hurricane Matthew traveled rapidly towards the southeastern region of the United States, it hit closely to the coasts of Florida, South Carolina, Georgia, and North Carolina. On October 7 in Fernandina Beach, Florida, there was a peak surge of 9.88\xc2\xa0ft (3.01\xc2\xa0m) above normal. Additionally, in the St. Augustine area, water was reported to be 2.5\xc2\xa0ft (0.76\xc2\xa0m) above ground.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup></p>\n<p>As Matthew tracked parallel to the Florida coast, it left over one million people without power across the state of Florida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">Jacksonville</a> it caused major sand dune damage and flooding in the <a href="/wiki/St._Johns_River" title="St. Johns River">St. Johns River</a>. It also destroyed many properties and knocked out power for nearly 250,000 electrical customers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matthew_hits_First_Coast_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-Matthew_hits_First_Coast-126">[125]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Indialantic,_Florida" title="Indialantic, Florida">Indialantic, Florida</a>, firefighters exposed themselves to the storm\'s winds to put out a fire, which reportedly destroyed a greenhouse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> In Florida, one woman died due to a heart attack; she had called for aid, but medical services were not able to arrive due to Matthew\'s high winds. Another two women were killed by falling trees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flagler_Beach" title="Flagler Beach">Flagler Beach</a> area, a portion of <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Road_A1A" title="Florida State Road A1A">Florida State Road A1A</a> was washed away.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">Kennedy Space Center</a>, winds reached 80\xc2\xa0mph (130\xc2\xa0km/h) at ground level while a gust of 136\xc2\xa0mph (219\xc2\xa0km/h) was observed atop a 500\xc2\xa0ft (150\xc2\xa0m) tower. The facility suffered several million dollars-worth of damage, though overall impacts were less than anticipated. The roof of Operations Support Building II broke, and rainwater damaged the interior. Air conditioning was lost throughout <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39" title="Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39">Launch Complex 39</a> as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> The planned launches of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GOES-R" title="GOES-R">GOES-R</a>, NOAA\'s next generation weather satellite, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CYGNSS" title="CYGNSS">CYGNSS</a>, a cluster of smaller satellites which study hurricanes, were delayed due to the suspension of operations during Matthew.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Over 250,000 customers were left without power in Georgia after Hurricane Matthew affected the area. Roads were also blocked in the <a href="/wiki/Brunswick,_Georgia" title="Brunswick, Georgia">Brunswick, Georgia</a>, area, where all access points to <a href="/wiki/St._Simons,_Georgia" title="St. Simons, Georgia">St. Simons Island</a> were rendered impassable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bynum_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bynum-135">[134]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="North_and_South_Carolina">North and South Carolina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: North and South Carolina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Matthew_2016_Charleston,_South_Carolina,_flooding.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="5760" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Hurricane_Matthew_2016_Charleston%2C_South_Carolina%2C_flooding.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Matthew_2016_Charleston%2C_South_Carolina%2C_flooding.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Hurricane_Matthew_2016_Charleston%2C_South_Carolina%2C_flooding.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Matthew_2016_Charleston%2C_South_Carolina%2C_flooding.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Hurricane_Matthew_2016_Charleston%2C_South_Carolina%2C_flooding.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Matthew_2016_Charleston%2C_South_Carolina%2C_flooding.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Matthew_2016_Charleston,_South_Carolina,_flooding.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nFlooding in <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="Charleston, South Carolina">Charleston, South Carolina</a> on October\xc2\xa08.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Across South Carolina, at least 600,000 individuals lost power, where significant flooding was reported to have occurred in <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="Charleston, South Carolina">Charleston</a> after a seawall was breached.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hilton_Head_Island,_South_Carolina" title="Hilton Head Island, South Carolina">Hilton Head Island</a> experienced widespread water, sewer and power outages for several days, and the only road onto the island was not re-opened to residents until October 11. It is estimated that over 120,000 trees were downed on the island, causing extensive tree-strike damage to residences and businesses. Over 2.1 million cubic yards of vegetative debris generated by the storm was collected. The <a href="/wiki/Waccamaw_River" title="Waccamaw River">Waccamaw River</a> crested in <a href="/wiki/Conway,_South_Carolina" title="Conway, South Carolina">Conway</a> at 17.9\xc2\xa0ft (5.5\xc2\xa0m), breaking a record set by the <a href="/wiki/1928_Okeechobee_hurricane" title="1928 Okeechobee hurricane">1928 Okeechobee hurricane</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Little_Pee_Dee_River" title="Little Pee Dee River">Little Pee Dee River</a> reached a record crest of 17.1\xc2\xa0ft (5.2\xc2\xa0m) at <a href="/wiki/Galivants_Ferry,_South_Carolina" title="Galivants Ferry, South Carolina">Galivant\'s Ferry</a>, also breaking a 1928 record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Matthew_aftermath,_Greenville,_NC,_near_Pitt%E2%80%93Greenville_Airport_-_22.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2988" data-file-width="5312" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Hurricane_Matthew_aftermath%2C_Greenville%2C_NC%2C_near_Pitt%E2%80%93Greenville_Airport_-_22.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Matthew_aftermath%2C_Greenville%2C_NC%2C_near_Pitt%E2%80%93Greenville_Airport_-_22.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Hurricane_Matthew_aftermath%2C_Greenville%2C_NC%2C_near_Pitt%E2%80%93Greenville_Airport_-_22.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Matthew_aftermath%2C_Greenville%2C_NC%2C_near_Pitt%E2%80%93Greenville_Airport_-_22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Hurricane_Matthew_aftermath%2C_Greenville%2C_NC%2C_near_Pitt%E2%80%93Greenville_Airport_-_22.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Matthew_aftermath%2C_Greenville%2C_NC%2C_near_Pitt%E2%80%93Greenville_Airport_-_22.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Matthew_aftermath,_Greenville,_NC,_near_Pitt%E2%80%93Greenville_Airport_-_22.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Tar_River" title="Tar River">Tar River</a> overflowing its banks near <a href="/wiki/Pitt%E2%80%93Greenville_Airport" title="Pitt\xe2\x80\x93Greenville Airport">Pitt\xe2\x80\x93Greenville Airport</a> on October\xc2\xa012; it later crested at 24.5 feet (7.5\xc2\xa0m).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heather_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Heather-138">[137]</a></sup></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Twenty-six people died in storm-related incidents across North Carolina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NorthCarolina26deaths_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-NorthCarolina26deaths-116">[115]</a></sup> 680,000 in North Carolina were without power at one point.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> Sections of <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95" title="Interstate 95">Interstate 95</a> <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_South_Carolina" title="Interstate 95 in South Carolina">in South Carolina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_North_Carolina" title="Interstate 95 in North Carolina">in North Carolina</a> had to be shut down as a result of hurricane flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> The North Carolina section reopened October 17.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> After 10\xc2\xa0in (25\xc2\xa0cm) of rain fell in <a href="/wiki/Cumberland_County,_North_Carolina" title="Cumberland County, North Carolina">Cumberland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harnett_County,_North_Carolina" title="Harnett County, North Carolina">Harnett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hoke_County,_North_Carolina" title="Hoke County, North Carolina">Hoke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moore_County,_North_Carolina" title="Moore County, North Carolina">Moore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robeson_County,_North_Carolina" title="Robeson County, North Carolina">Robeson Counties</a> on September 28 causing flooding, Matthew dumped another 10\xc2\xa0in (25\xc2\xa0cm) to 14\xc2\xa0in (36\xc2\xa0cm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup> As a result, the <a href="/wiki/Lumber_River" title="Lumber River">Lumber River</a> reached a record 24\xc2\xa0ft (7.3\xc2\xa0m) in the south end of <a href="/wiki/Lumberton,_North_Carolina" title="Lumberton, North Carolina">Lumberton</a>, breaking the record of 20.5\xc2\xa0ft (6.2\xc2\xa0m) feet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup> Robeson County schools did not reopen until October 31.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCrory_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-McCrory-144">[143]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Smithfield,_North_Carolina" title="Smithfield, North Carolina">Smithfield</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Neuse_River" title="Neuse River">Neuse River</a> crested at 29.09\xc2\xa0ft (8.87\xc2\xa0m), 2\xc2\xa0ft (0.61\xc2\xa0m) higher than after <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Fran" title="Hurricane Fran">Hurricane Fran</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Kinston,_North_Carolina" title="Kinston, North Carolina">Kinston</a>, the Neuse crested at 28.31\xc2\xa0ft (8.63\xc2\xa0m), a foot (300\xc2\xa0mm) higher than the record set by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Floyd" title="Hurricane Floyd">Hurricane Floyd</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Greenville,_North_Carolina" title="Greenville, North Carolina">Greenville</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Tar_River" title="Tar River">Tar River</a> crested at 24.5\xc2\xa0ft (7.5\xc2\xa0m).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heather_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-Heather-138">[137]</a></sup> Preliminary estimates indicate that roughly 100,000\xc2\xa0structures were flooded across the state and damage reached US$1.5\xc2\xa0billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Virginia_and_the_Northeast">Virginia and the Northeast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Virginia and the Northeast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Matthew_damage_in_Lago_Mar,_Virginia_Beach,_Virginia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2432" data-file-width="4320" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Hurricane_Matthew_damage_in_Lago_Mar%2C_Virginia_Beach%2C_Virginia.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Matthew_damage_in_Lago_Mar%2C_Virginia_Beach%2C_Virginia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Hurricane_Matthew_damage_in_Lago_Mar%2C_Virginia_Beach%2C_Virginia.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Matthew_damage_in_Lago_Mar%2C_Virginia_Beach%2C_Virginia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Hurricane_Matthew_damage_in_Lago_Mar%2C_Virginia_Beach%2C_Virginia.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Matthew_damage_in_Lago_Mar%2C_Virginia_Beach%2C_Virginia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Matthew_damage_in_Lago_Mar,_Virginia_Beach,_Virginia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nHeavy rains and high winds resulted in trees falling and record flooding in <a href="/wiki/Lago_Mar,_Virginia_Beach,_Virginia" title="Lago Mar, Virginia Beach, Virginia">Lago Mar, Virginia Beach, Virginia</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>When the hurricane hit Virginia, Matthew caused two deaths and street flooding in the eastern part of the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-122">[121]</a></sup> The Northeast received heavy rain and minor flooding throughout the days of October 9 and 10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Matthew_from_Hurricane_to_Post-Tropical_2016-10-06_to_11.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="571" data-file-width="671" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Matthew_from_Hurricane_to_Post-Tropical_2016-10-06_to_11.gif/220px-Matthew_from_Hurricane_to_Post-Tropical_2016-10-06_to_11.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Matthew_from_Hurricane_to_Post-Tropical_2016-10-06_to_11.gif/330px-Matthew_from_Hurricane_to_Post-Tropical_2016-10-06_to_11.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Matthew_from_Hurricane_to_Post-Tropical_2016-10-06_to_11.gif/440px-Matthew_from_Hurricane_to_Post-Tropical_2016-10-06_to_11.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Matthew_from_Hurricane_to_Post-Tropical_2016-10-06_to_11.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nSatellite image loop from October 6, when Matthew was a hurricane, to October 11, when it had joined a mid-latitude storm sweeping across eastern Canada.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Matthew\'s post-tropical remains were absorbed into a frontal zone off the coast of North Carolina. The humidity of the tropical system was drawn into the storm that was formed then. The latter gave heavy rain and strong winds in <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island" title="Prince Edward Island">Prince Edward Island</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newfoundland" title="Newfoundland">Newfoundland</a> from October 10 to 11.</p>\n<p>In Nova Scotia, rain amounts were recorded from east to west as 8.85\xc2\xa0in (224.8\xc2\xa0mm) in <a href="/wiki/Sydney,_Nova_Scotia" title="Sydney, Nova Scotia">Sydney</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Island" title="Cape Breton Island">Cape Breton Island</a>), 5.09\xc2\xa0in (129.2\xc2\xa0mm) in <a href="/wiki/Port_Hawkesbury" title="Port Hawkesbury">Port Hawkesbury</a>, 4.50\xc2\xa0in (114.4\xc2\xa0mm) in <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A9ticamp,_Nova_Scotia" title="Ch\xc3\xa9ticamp, Nova Scotia">Ch\xc3\xa9ticamp</a>, 4.05\xc2\xa0in (102.8\xc2\xa0mm) in <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_Nova_Scotia" title="Halifax, Nova Scotia">Halifax</a>, 3.263\xc2\xa0in (82.88\xc2\xa0mm) in Kentville, and 1.94\xc2\xa0in (49.2\xc2\xa0mm) in <a href="/wiki/Yarmouth,_Nova_Scotia" title="Yarmouth, Nova Scotia">Yarmouth</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SRC-NS_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-SRC-NS-150">[149]</a></sup> Heavy rains and strong winds caused flooding and dangerous conditions, particularly in the counties of Pictou, Antigonish, Guysborough and Cape Breton. Several roads were closed to heavy trucks, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Halifax_Port_Authority" title="Halifax Port Authority">Halifax Harbour</a> bridges and the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_Bridge" title="Confederation Bridge">Confederation Bridge</a> between New Brunswick and Prince Edward Island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SRC-NS_150-1"><a href="#cite_note-SRC-NS-150">[149]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Newfoundland was even more affected with accumulations generally ranging from 3.9 to 5.9\xc2\xa0in (100 to 150\xc2\xa0mm) in the central, southern and western areas. Steady rain fell sometimes at a rate of 0.39 to 0.79\xc2\xa0in (10 to 20\xc2\xa0mm) per hour, and even 1.7\xc2\xa0in (42\xc2\xa0mm) per hour in <a href="/wiki/Burgeo" title="Burgeo">Burgeo</a>. A private station in that community recorded a total of 9.23\xc2\xa0in (234.4\xc2\xa0mm), while the official station of the <a href="/wiki/Gander_International_Airport" title="Gander International Airport">Gander International Airport</a> signaled 6.45\xc2\xa0in (163.8\xc2\xa0mm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SRC-TN_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-SRC-TN-151">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMC_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-SMC-152">[151]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The rain caused numerous landslides and swollen rivers cut roads. The state of emergency was declared in <a href="/wiki/Lewisporte" title="Lewisporte">Lewisporte</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Alban%27s,_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="St. Alban\'s, Newfoundland and Labrador">St. Alban\'s</a> and <a href="/wiki/Little_Burnt_Bay" title="Little Burnt Bay">Little Burnt Bay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBC_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-CBC-153">[152]</a></sup> The town of St. Alban\'s, a community of about 1,200, was cut off from the surrounding communities when the main bridge in town was carried by the waters and a nearby community (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conne_River" title="Conne River">Conne River</a>) provided a boat to transport people to St. Alban\'s and out of the community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBC_153-1"><a href="#cite_note-CBC-153">[152]</a></sup> The highway to Burgeo, on the south coast of Newfoundland, was also flooded and had to be closed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SRC-TN_151-1"><a href="#cite_note-SRC-TN-151">[150]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The winds of over 56\xc2\xa0mph (90\xc2\xa0km/h) also caused many fallen trees and electric power outages. The official maximum winds were recorded in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port_aux_Basques" title="Port aux Basques">Port aux Basques</a> at 80\xc2\xa0mph (128\xc2\xa0km/h) and informally in Green Island, <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Bay" title="Fortune Bay">Fortune Bay</a>, at 81\xc2\xa0mph (130\xc2\xa0km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SRC-TN_151-2"><a href="#cite_note-SRC-TN-151">[150]</a></sup> Damage to roads across Newfoundland was assessed in excess of CA$10\xc2\xa0million (US$7.6\xc2\xa0million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBC_News_-_14-10-2016_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-CBC_News_-_14-10-2016-77">[76]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lesser_Antilles_2">Lesser Antilles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Lesser Antilles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In Martinique, <a href="/wiki/%C3%89lectricit%C3%A9_de_France" title="\xc3\x89lectricit\xc3\xa9 de France">\xc3\x89lectricit\xc3\xa9 de France</a> requested additional crews from <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a> to help restore power. Members of the military and Forces fran\xc3\xa7aises aux Antilles were deployed to assist in clearing debris from roadways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LCISep30_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-LCISep30-84">[83]</a></sup> The St. Lucia Red Cross distributed non-food items to 270\xc2\xa0people affected by the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Haiti_3">Haiti</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Haiti">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_CH-53E_Sea_Stallion_helicopter_lands_aboard_USS_Mesa_Verde._(29564408643).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1996" data-file-width="3000" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/A_CH-53E_Sea_Stallion_helicopter_lands_aboard_USS_Mesa_Verde._%2829564408643%29.jpg/220px-A_CH-53E_Sea_Stallion_helicopter_lands_aboard_USS_Mesa_Verde._%2829564408643%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/A_CH-53E_Sea_Stallion_helicopter_lands_aboard_USS_Mesa_Verde._%2829564408643%29.jpg/330px-A_CH-53E_Sea_Stallion_helicopter_lands_aboard_USS_Mesa_Verde._%2829564408643%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/A_CH-53E_Sea_Stallion_helicopter_lands_aboard_USS_Mesa_Verde._%2829564408643%29.jpg/440px-A_CH-53E_Sea_Stallion_helicopter_lands_aboard_USS_Mesa_Verde._%2829564408643%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_CH-53E_Sea_Stallion_helicopter_lands_aboard_USS_Mesa_Verde._(29564408643).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA CH-53E Sea Stallion helicopter assigned to the 24th <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marine_Expeditionary_Unit" title="Marine Expeditionary Unit">Marine Expeditionary Unit</a>, lands on the flight deck of the amphibious transport dock ship <a href="/wiki/USS_Mesa_Verde" title="USS Mesa Verde">USS\xc2\xa0<i>Mesa Verde</i></a>. It is underway in preparation to support humanitarian assistance and disaster relief efforts in Haiti in response to Hurricane Matthew</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>On October\xc2\xa04, the United States prepared the aircraft carrier, the hospital ship <a href="/wiki/USNS_Comfort_(T-AH-20)" title="USNS Comfort (T-AH-20)">USNS\xc2\xa0<i>Comfort</i></a>\xe2\x80\x94which previously aided thousands in the wake of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">2010 Haiti earthquake</a>\xe2\x80\x94and the transport dock for relief operations in Haiti. <a href="/wiki/USS_Mesa_Verde" title="USS Mesa Verde">USS\xc2\xa0<i>Mesa Verde</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/USS_George_Washington_(CVN-73)" title="USS George Washington (CVN-73)">USS\xc2\xa0<i>George Washington</i></a> were later relieved by <a href="/wiki/USS_Iwo_Jima_(LHD-7)" title="USS Iwo Jima (LHD-7)">USS\xc2\xa0<i>Iwo Jima</i></a>, along with the 24th <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marine_Expeditionary_Unit" title="Marine Expeditionary Unit">Marine Expeditionary Unit</a>. <a href="/wiki/United_States_Southern_Command" title="United States Southern Command">United States Southern Command</a> also deployed 100\xc2\xa0troops with 9\xc2\xa0helicopters to the Cayman Islands to prepare for relief work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup> Initial estimates indicated at least 350,000\xc2\xa0people were in need of assistance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCOct6_93-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBCOct6-93">[92]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The bridge between the south and Port-au-Prince was destroyed. As a result, aid agencies reported they were having difficulty getting around to the most damaged and storm-affected parts of Haiti.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The commander of U.S. forces in the Caribbean reported that troops and 6 helicopters from <a href="/wiki/Joint_Task_Force_Bravo" title="Joint Task Force Bravo">Joint Task Force-Bravo</a> had been deployed to Haiti for the aftermath, and were expected to arrive on October\xc2\xa06. These are expected to help with search-and-rescue missions as well as providing medical assistance. In addition to his, a one-star navy admiral will also travel to lead the task force involved in the operations. More than 300 military personnel will most likely travel to Haiti, with 300 Marines on board on the ships sent out for aid from the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weather1_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-weather1-157">[156]</a></sup></p>\n<p>A number of aid agencies deployed to Haiti to help with the aftermath:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup></p>\n<ul>\n<li>Action Aid reported that over 50,000 people were in immediate need of clean water and shelters.</li>\n<li>World Nation also sent out helicopters, reporting difficulties and their concern about young children and food. They will be providing water and sanitation for over 50,000 people.</li>\n<li>The UN\'s World Food Program arranged for enough food to feed up to 300,000 people for a month. A further 34 tonnes are ready in Miami to be used if needed.</li>\n<li>UNICEF will be providing life-saving aid for 10,000 people.</li>\n<li>UN\'s Food and Agricultural Organisation said it would be helping farmers rebuild their businesses by providing seeds.</li>\n<li>The US Agency for International Development said it would provide $400,000 for aid to Jamaica and Haiti on October\xc2\xa03.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Red Cross launched a campaign to raise $9.6 million to provide water, shelter, and food for 50,000 people. They also sent a large number of local volunteers to the south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-92">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[159]</a></sup></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuba_2">Cuba</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Cuba">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a> coordinated with the Government of Cuba to provide food to approximately 180,000\xc2\xa0people in need across eastern provinces. The operation would span six months and cost US$4\xc2\xa0million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[160]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_3">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Matthew_2016_Fayetteville,_North_Carolina,_National_Guard_rescue.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="664" data-file-width="1000" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Hurricane_Matthew_2016_Fayetteville%2C_North_Carolina%2C_National_Guard_rescue.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Matthew_2016_Fayetteville%2C_North_Carolina%2C_National_Guard_rescue.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Hurricane_Matthew_2016_Fayetteville%2C_North_Carolina%2C_National_Guard_rescue.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Matthew_2016_Fayetteville%2C_North_Carolina%2C_National_Guard_rescue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Hurricane_Matthew_2016_Fayetteville%2C_North_Carolina%2C_National_Guard_rescue.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Matthew_2016_Fayetteville%2C_North_Carolina%2C_National_Guard_rescue.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Matthew_2016_Fayetteville,_North_Carolina,_National_Guard_rescue.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_National_Guard" title="North Carolina National Guard">North Carolina National Guard</a> assisting with high-water rescues in <a href="/wiki/Fayetteville,_North_Carolina" title="Fayetteville, North Carolina">Fayetteville, North Carolina</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In Georgia, the Governor retracted previous evacuations later, emphasizing that their lives could not be endangered for those who chose not to leave. 1,000 members of the National Guard were deployed for help later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[161]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In North Carolina, nearly 900 people had been rescued by boat crews by the morning of October\xc2\xa09.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup> In April\xc2\xa02017, North Carolina Governor Roy Cooper requested $929\xc2\xa0million in federal funds. The following month, the Trump administration denied more than 99\xc2\xa0percent of this request and only provided $6.1\xc2\xa0million to the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[163]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retirement">Retirement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Retirement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Atlantic_hurricane_names" title="List of retired Atlantic hurricane names">List of retired Atlantic hurricane names</a></div>\n<p>On March\xc2\xa026, 2017, it was announced by the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a> that the name <i>Matthew</i> was retired due to the extensive damage and loss of life it caused along its track, particularly in Haiti, Cuba, and the United States, and will never again be used to name an <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_hurricane" title="Atlantic hurricane">Atlantic hurricane</a>. It will be replaced with <i>Martin</i> for the 2022 Atlantic hurricane season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em href="/wiki/List_of_North_Carolina_hurricanes_(2000%E2%80%93present)" title="List of North Carolina hurricanes (2000\xe2\x80\x93present)">List of North Carolina hurricanes (2000\xe2\x80\x93present)</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hazel" title="Hurricane Hazel">Hurricane Hazel</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Took a similar track through the Caribbean in 1954, and struck North Carolina as a Category\xc2\xa04 hurricane.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_David" title="Hurricane David">Hurricane David</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Made landfall in the Dominican Republic as a Category 5 before skirting the eastern coast of Florida in 1979.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Tomas" title="Hurricane Tomas">Hurricane Tomas</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Traced a slightly similar path in the Caribbean, but stayed out to sea rather than curving towards the United States after impacting Hispaniola in 2010.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Joaquin" title="Hurricane Joaquin">Hurricane Joaquin</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Ravaged the Central Bahamas roughly a year before Matthew.</li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Matthew&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Although <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sandy" title="Hurricane Sandy">Hurricane Sandy</a> was significantly deeper and made landfall much farther north in late October 2012, it was an <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclone</a> at the time of landfall.</span></li>\n</ol>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
